item_0.note: Case Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022 involves Debra Marshall and centers on whether to file a motion for a trial date or pursue mediation in her motor vehicle accident matter. The discussion concluded that a motion for a trial date will be filed if no resolution is reached by Friday.

In a planning conversation, attorney Aaron Wy spoke with Ann Dattillo about two options: filing a motion for a trial date or pursuing mediation. They agreed that if no decision is made by Friday, they will file the motion for a trial to secure a firm date.

Ann inquired about whether Debra (Debbie) would need to be present at the trial. Aaron clarified that while she would likely need to be there, he is not keen on going to trial due to her emotional instability.

They also agreed that if mediation occurs, it would likely be conducted over the phone or via Zoom, which would be more convenient for Ann.

Action items: Aaron Wy will file a motion for a trial date if no resolution is reached by Friday. Ann Dattillo will arrange travel for Debra if the trial proceeds.

item_1.note: Case Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022 involves client Debra Marshall. The latest conversation provided an update on Mr. Marshall’s legal case, detailing progress toward mediation and the next steps.

According to the update from Aaron Whaley, all initial discovery has been completed, and the team will send the defense attorney all medical records and bills by the end of the week or next week. Once the defense attorney reviews the documents, they will schedule a mediation date in an effort to settle the case. Aaron explained that estimating a monetary value for the case is challenging due to disputes over liability and the nature of the injuries. There is a risk of receiving nothing, but there is also a significant incentive for the opposing party to negotiate because of high medical bills.

The tasks outlined are: Aaron Whaley will send all medical records and bills to the defense attorney by the end of the week or next week, and Aaron will follow up to schedule a mediation date once the defense attorney has reviewed the documents.

item_37.note: In the Debra Marshall v Jasmine Reed matter, Barren County Circuit Court case number 23-CI-00659 (the file also references Debra Marshall’s motor vehicle accident on December 3, 2022, labeled Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022), The Whaley Law Firm prepared and sent a Notice to Take Deposition of Jasmine Reed. The notice was filed via CourtNet and carried envelope number 9684744. The transmission came from Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, located at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with direct dial [PHONE-68] and main office line [PHONE-417] ext. 104. Her email address noted on the message was Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (marked as the new email address). The recipient was Hensley & Ross, Attorneys at Law, at 207 E. Main St., P.O. Box 350, Horse Cave, KY 42749, with the firm’s phone number [PHONE-416] and fax [PHONE-71].

The scheduling of depositions progressed through a lengthy email chain beginning in December 2024. On December 20, 2024, Sarena Tuttle stated that, after a quick review of the file, the parties were ready to schedule the deposition of Mrs. Reed and asked for dates when Jasmine Reed and Hensley & Ross could participate via Zoom, inviting any questions and even offering settlement discussions if an offer was being considered to move the matter forward. In the subsequent exchanges on January 13, 2025, Sarena reminded that on December 20, 2024 she had reached out for deposition dates and noted that the matter was approaching 30 days without a response; she requested dates for depositions via Zoom and indicated openness to settlement discussions if appropriate. Pat Hensley of Hensley & Ross replied that he would need to check with his client and proposed dates of February 17, 19, 20, or 21. Sarena acknowledged, and Pat added that his client would be available Mondays, explaining that the defendant’s schedule was constrained by his client’s nursing school.

The conversation continued with further back-and-forth in mid-January 2025. On January 13, 2025, Sarena confirmed that the February dates would need to be weighed and indicated that the March dates might be workable. Pat responded that his client would be available on Mondays for scheduling, proposing March 3 or March 10 as possibilities. Sarena then suggested that 1:30 p.m. could work and asked whether a 10:00 a.m. start for Debra Marshall would be feasible, noting that Zoom would be used for the depositions. Pat asked whether the proceedings would be remote and whether Debra Marshall would be available. Sarena replied affirmatively to the remote format and the 1:30 p.m. time, and suggested starting Mrs. Marshall at 10:00 a.m. EST. The parties continued to discuss the plan, with the understanding that the March 3 date remained a viable option.

By January 17, 2025, the scheduling had crystallized further: the plan was for March 3, 2025, with Jasmine Reed’s deposition at 1:30 p.m. via Zoom, and the plaintiff’s deposition to be held via Zoom as well with a start time to be confirmed. At roughly the same time, Hensley & Ross suggested a start time of 10:30 a.m. for the plaintiff’s deposition, and Sarena indicated she would send the notice shortly. Later that day, Sarena confirmed the plan and issued the deposition notice: “Here is our Notice to Take Deposition of Jasmine Reed, filed via CourtNet Envelope 9684744 moments ago,” accompanied by the sender’s details and the reminder to use the new email address. The notice was sent to Hensley & Ross, with the expectation that the depositions would proceed by Zoom on March 3, 2025, Reed at 1:30 p.m. and the plaintiff at 10:30 a.m., both to be conducted remotely. The communications also recorded that the notice was filed via CourtNet and included the exchange history and the participants’ contact information, including Sarena’s updated email address.

item_40.note: Case: Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022. Client: Debra Marshall. This note covers communications about a new scheduling submission related to Debra Marshall’s motor vehicle accident matter.

item_43.note: This narrative summarizes the scheduling communications between The Whaley Law Firm (representing the plaintiff, Debra Marshall) and Hensley & Ross (representing the defendant, Jasmine Reed) in Debra Marshall v. Jasmine Reed, Barren County Circuit Court, Case 23-CI-00659. The case caption shows Debra Marshall as the plaintiff with a motor vehicle accident date of December 3, 2022 (Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022). The depositions under discussion were to be conducted by Zoom, with the defendant’s deposition of Jasmine Reed set for March 3, 2025 at 1:30 p.m. and the plaintiff Debra Marshall’s deposition to be scheduled for an earlier time on the same day.

The exchange began with an email on December 20, 2024, from Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; D: [PHONE-403]; O: [PHONE-402] ext 104; E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com; note: new email address) to Pat Hensley of Hensley & Ross (207 E. Main St., P.O. Box 350, Horse Cave, KY 42749; [PHONE-401]; fax [PHONE-400]). Tuttle stated that they had previously reached out and were awaiting dates for deposing Mrs. Reed, proposing that the depositions be conducted via Zoom and that they were open to settlement if the other side wished to make an offer instead of providing deposition dates. In addition, she noted that they were looking to avoid further delays and invited discussion on settlement if appropriate.

On January 13, 2025, Tuttle responded to Hensley & Ross, noting that from the dates previously discussed, only February 20, 2025 worked for The Whaley Law Firm, with a March schedule that could be fairly open if needed. Hensley & Ross replied later that day, offering February 17, 19, 20, or 21 as alternatives and indicating they would need to check with their client. Tuttle then stated that of those dates, February 20 works for them, reiterating the possibility of a open March schedule if needed. Hensley & Ross followed up, saying they would confirm with their client. The firm then added that their client (Debra Marshall) is starting nursing school and is only available on Mondays, proposing March 3 or March 10 as options. 

On January 15, 2025, Tuttle indicated that a 1:30 p.m. start time was acceptable for Reed and suggested that Zoom would be a good format for this matter. She also asked whether Debra Marshall could be available that morning and whether they should start her deposition at 10:00 a.m. EST. Hensley & Ross asked for confirmation that the 1:30 p.m. time would work and whether the deposition would be conducted remotely, inquiring about the availability of their client on that schedule. Tuttle reaffirmed that 1:30 p.m. would work, that Zoom was suitable, and that Debra Marshall would be available that morning with an intended 10:00 a.m. start for her deposition, noting that the March 3, 2025 date would accommodate Reed’s 1:30 p.m. deposition via Zoom and that the plaintiff’s start time remained to be confirmed. 

On January 17, 2025, Hensley & Ross proposed finalizing the plaintiff’s start time at 10:30 a.m. EST, while keeping Jasmine Reed’s deposition for March 3, 2025 at 1:30 p.m. via Zoom. Sarena Tuttle then replied to confirm the March 3, 2025 schedule with Reed at 1:30 p.m. via Zoom and to request the plaintiff’s start time, noting that both depositions would be conducted via Zoom. The thread closes with Hensley & Ross confirming the 10:30 a.m. EST start for the plaintiff’s deposition and the 1:30 p.m. start for Reed on March 3, 2025.

Throughout these emails, the parties reference the following contact details and signatures:

- Hensley & Ross, Attorneys at Law
  207 E. Main St.
  P.O. Box 350
  Horse Cave, KY 42749
  [PHONE-87]
  fax [PHONE-88]

  Louisville, KY 40222

item_44.note: In the Debra Marshall v Jasmine Reed matter (Barren County Circuit Court, 23-CI-00659), which stems from a motor vehicle accident on December 3, 2022, Debra Marshall is represented by The Whaley Law Firm, and Jasmine Reed is represented by Hensley & Ross. On December 20, 2024, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager for The Whaley Law Firm (contactable at Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com and at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; D: [PHONE-395]; O: [PHONE-394] ext. 104), emailed Pat Ross of Hensley & Ross (to [EMAIL-93]) requesting dates on which Jasmine Reed and the firm could depose Mrs. Reed via Zoom. She noted that the Whaley firm had previously reached out about deposition dates and had not received a response for nearly 30 days. Sarena responded that February 20 would work for them and that they had a fairly open schedule for March if that helped. Hensley & Ross reiterated their Monday-only constraint and proposed those March dates.

Throughout January 2025, Sarena and Pat continued to discuss preferred start times. At one point Sarena asked whether a 1:00 p.m. EST start would be acceptable, and later conversations anchored on a 1:30 p.m. start for the deposition of Jasmine Reed, with Zoom identified as the method. In a January 15, 2025 exchange, Hensley & Ross asked if Reed’s 1:30 p.m. start would work and whether the deposition could be conducted remotely, also inquiring about Debra Marshall’s availability.

On January 15, 2025, Sarena raised the possibility of a 1:00 p.m. EST start and noted the option of a 1:30 p.m. start, with Zoom as the preferred platform. By January 15, 2025 at 11:04 a.m., the parties appeared to converge on a plan: a 1:30 p.m. start for Jasmine Reed via Zoom, with Debra Marshall’s deposition also to be conducted via Zoom, and with Debra Marshall available that morning if a 10:00 a.m. EST start for her deposition was workable for the other side.

Finally, on January 17, 2025 at 1:16 p.m. (Eastern Time), Sarena Tuttle followed up to finalize the scheduling. The recap stated that, on March 3, 2025, Jasmine Reed would be deposed at 1:30 p.m. via Zoom, and that the Plaintiff’s deposition would also be conducted via Zoom at a time to be confirmed. She asked what start time would work best for beginning Debra Marshall’s deposition.

The latest scheduling communications also include contact details for Sarena Tuttle, who has a new email address (Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com), and reiterate the firm’s Louisville office at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222. The Whaley Law Firm’s phone numbers are listed as D: [PHONE-392] and O: [PHONE-391] ext. 104, and the firm’s email is provided for further coordination.

In summary, the deposition schedule as of the latest communications is set for March 3, 2025, with Jasmine Reed’s deposition at 1:30 p.m. via Zoom, and Debra Marshall’s deposition to be conducted via Zoom in the morning, with an exact start time to be confirmed. The parties remain aligned on Zoom as the deposition method and are awaiting final confirmation of the Plaintiff’s start time.

item_129.note: Case: Debra Marshall v. Jasmine Reed, in the Barren Circuit Court (case number 23-CI-00659). The matter stems from a motor vehicle accident on December 3, 2022, and the client is Debra Marshall. Debra Marshall is represented by The Whaley Law Firm, with W. Bryce Koon, Esq., handling the matter. The following is a narrative summary of the discovery-related correspondence between The Whaley Law Firm and Hensley & Ross, along with related context.

In late January 2024, The Whaley Law Firm began a series of communications regarding discovery. On January 23, 2024, Bryce Koon emailed Patrick Hensley of Hensley & Ross, noting that discovery requests had been served contemporaneously with the Complaint and asking when the responses could be expected. He offered to provide an extension if needed or to send the discovery requests himself. He also informed Hensley & Ross that KFB, acting for Edie Renick, had filed a property damage claim in Barren District Court against Debra Marshall. He indicated that he had filed a motion to consolidate that property damage case with the Debra Marshall v. Jasmine Reed matter, which would be heard that day and would likely face no objection. He invited any questions regarding these matters.

On January 26, 2024, at 12:05 PM, Bryce Koon replied that a 30-day extension would be fine. Later that day, at 12:45 PM, Hensley & Ross responded: “Bryce: Thank you for agreeing to grant me additional time to respond to the discovery served with the complaint. If you could give me another 30 days that should be sufficient.” On January 29, 2024, at 12:26 PM, Hensley & Ross sent a brief acknowledgment: “Thanks.”

Moving forward, on March 19, 2024, at 10:39 AM, Bryce Koon asked for an update on the outstanding discovery requests. That same day, at 4:46 PM, Hensley & Ross replied: “Like always I am running behind. I will get in touch with her and get those answered within the near future. Thanks.”

On April 9, 2024, at 12:48 PM, Bryce Koon wrote again, stating: “Good afternoon counsel, I am writing again to determine when we may expect your client’s discovery responses. It appears these requests have been outstanding for some time now.” Later that day, at 2:34 PM, Hensley & Ross replied: “I apologize for the delay. I have been having trouble getting in touch with my client. I will try a different avenue.”

Finally, on May 31, 2024, at 2:59 PM, Bryce Koon followed up once more: “Counsel, It has been quite some time, so I thought I would follow up on this one again. Please advise when we may expect your client’s discovery answers in this regard.” Each message in this sequence contains the standard confidentiality disclaimer typical of the sending firm.

In summary, the record shows a back-and-forth over several months (January through May 2024) concerning the timing of discovery responses in Debra Marshall’s case against Jasmine Reed, with parallel reference to a related property damage claim involving Edie Renick and a motion to consolidate that claim with the Debra Marshall case. The exchanges reflect multiple extensions requested and granted, ongoing difficulties contacting the client, and repeated follow-ups from The Whaley Law Firm seeking production of discovery responses.

Marshall.” The message included a caution that the email was from an external source and advised not to open attachments or click links from an unknown or suspicious origin, and it then asked, “Thank you so much. If the communication was received in error, the recipient was instructed to notify the sender immediately and to delete or destroy the material and information. This Privacy Notice appeared twice in the email.

Additionally, the correspondence from Tamara Shive included her signature line and the organization’s website, http://www.tjregionalhealth.org. Finally, at 5:36:55 PM on the same day, Tamara Shive clarified in a separate note that, “Yes, billing will always arrive separately, as it is another department.”

item_149.note: This note concerns the motor vehicle accident case Debra Marshall v. Jasmine Reed, docketed as Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022, with Debra Marshall as the client. item_152.note: Case: Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022. Client: Debra Marshall. The matter is Debra Marshall v. Jasmine Reed in the Barren Circuit Court, docket 23-CI-00659. The following notes summarize the email communications between The Whaley Law Firm and the law firm Hensley & Ross regarding discovery responses, set in the context of Debra Marshall’s motor vehicle accident case against Jasmine Reed.

The exchange begins with an email dated January 23, 2024. W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm (Louisville, Kentucky) wrote to Patrick Hensley of Hensley & Ross, with copies to Sarena Tuttle and Debra Marshall’s file-service address, explaining that discovery requests had been served contemporaneously with the Complaint and asking when the opposing side could be expected to provide responses. He offered to extend time if needed or to resend the discovery if necessary. Koon also noted that KFB (on behalf of Edie Renick) had filed a property damage claim in Barren District Court against his client, and that he had filed a motion to consolidate that case with the Debra Marshall v. Jasmine Reed action, which was to be heard that day and would likely face no objection. He invited any questions and signed with his contact information and the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer.

On January 26, 2024, at 12:05 PM, Koon replied to Hensley & Ross with: “30 days should be fine.” He again provided his contact details. Later that same day, at 12:45 PM, Hensley & Ross replied: “Bryce: Thank you for agreeing to grant me additional time to respond to the discovery served with the complaint. If you could give me another 30 days that should be sufficient.” Pat of Hensley & Ross closed with their firm’s address and contact information, accompanied by the standard disclaimer about privileged information.

On January 29, 2024, Hensley & Ross sent a brief reply simply saying, “Thanks,” followed by the firm’s mailing address and contact details, again with the customary disclaimer.

The next sequence of correspondence occurred on March 19, 2024. At 10:39 AM, Bryce Koon sent an email to Hensley & Ross, addressed for counsel, cc’ing Debra Marshall’s file address, inquiring: “Good afternoon counsel, Just wanted to get an update on the outstanding requests.” He signed again as W. Bryce Koon, Esq., The Whaley Law Firm, with the usual contact information and privilege disclaimer.

That same day, March 19, 2024, at 4:46 PM, Hensley & Ross replied: “Like always I am running behind. I will get in touch with her and get those answered within the near future.” The message carried the firm’s standard signature lines and disclaimer.

Finally, on April 9, 2024, at 1:48 PM (Eastern Time, -0400), Bryce Koon sent another message to counsel: “Good afternoon counsel, I am writing again to determine when we may expect your client’s discovery responses. It appears these requests have been outstanding for some time now.” He concluded with his signature block for The Whaley Law Firm, Louisville, KY, and the same standard privilege disclaimer.

Throughout these exchanges, the subject line consistently referenced Debra Marshall v. Jasmine Reed (Barren Circuit 23-CI-00659). The communications include the parties and counsel identified above, the case identity, the discovery timeline discussions, and the motion to consolidate a separate property damage claim filed in Barren District Court (KFB, on behalf of Edie Renick) with the Debra Marshall matter, all set against the backdrop of a motor vehicle accident occurring on December 3, 2022. Each email ends with the customary attorney-client privilege disclaimer and the sender’s contact information.

Box 350, Horse Cave, KY 42749, and contact information: phone [PHONE-311], fax [PHONE-312]. The message also contained the standard privilege disclaimer.

On January 29, 2024, at 12:26 PM, Hensley & Ross again emailed Bryce Koon in the Debra Marshall v. Jasmine Reed matter. The body of that message consisted of a brief “Thanks,” and, as with the other emails, included the firm’s contact details and the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer.

Across all messages in the thread, the subject consistently appeared as Debra Marshall v. Jasmine Reed (Barren Circuit 23-CI-00659). The communications reflect discovery timing concerns and the parties’ negotiations over extending deadlines for responses to discovery, as well as a contemporaneous notice of a related property-damage case and an attempted consolidation. item_190.note: Case: Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022
Client: Debra Marshall

The note records a series of email exchanges concerning the caption KFBMIC (a/s/0 Edie Renick) v. Debra Marshall, pending in Barren District Court under docket 23-C-01110. The matter involves Debra Marshall as the client and Edie Renick’s related claim. The communications ran from late December 2023 through mid-January 2024 and included two law firms: John D. Bertram of Bertram, Camm & Bertram LLP (BCM LLP) representing Debra Marshall, and W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm representing KFBMIC. The discussions focused on whether district court and circuit court cases arising from the same facts should be consolidated, and on the status of filings and service.

Chronology and key details
- December 26, 2023, 9:37 a.m. (To: Bryce Koon; CC: Sarena Tuttle; Allan R. Bertram; Debby Bennett; Landon Cambron): John D. Bertram wrote, Good morning. He stated that he had been advised a separate matter had been filed in Barren Circuit Court, presumably arising from the same facts, and that he understood KFBMIC’s firm initiated that action. He asked John’s counterpart to confirm this understanding and whether the matters should be consolidated. He noted a presumed difference in damages (district court vs. circuit court) but suggested judicial economy might warrant consolidation, and he inquired whether an answer had been filed in the circuit matter.

- December 26, 2023, 2:05 p.m. (To: John Bertram; CC: Allan R. Bertram; Sarena Tuttle; Debby Bennett): Bryce Koon replied, stating that all of John’s presumptions were correct. He advised that a circuit court action had been filed against Jasmine Reed (the driver of Edie Renick’s vehicle) with Case No. 23-CI-00659. Reed had been served via certified mail on December 13, 2023, but no answer had been filed to date. Bryce indicated his intention to file a motion to consolidate the district court case into the circuit court case and asked whether John had any objections to the attached motion; he also offered to draft an agreed order.

- December 27, 2023, 9:37 a.m. (To: Bryce Koon; CC: Sarena Tuttle; Allan R. Bertram; Debby Bennett; Landon Cambron): John Bertram sent a follow-up, Good morning. He reiterated that a separate matter had been filed in Barren Circuit Court, presumably arising from the same facts, and that Bryce’s firm had initiated that action. He asked for confirmation and whether the matters should be consolidated, noting the potential damages difference and the possible efficiency gains from consolidation. He also asked whether an answer had been filed in the circuit matter.

- December 27, 2023, 10:02 a.m. (To: John Bertram; CC: Sarena Tuttle; Allan R. Bertram; Debby Bennett; Landon Cambron): Bryce Koon replied, Good morning John. He stated that all of John’s presumptions were correct: a circuit court action had been filed against Jasmine Reed (driver of Ms. Renick’s vehicle) – Case No. 23-CI-00659. Reed was served via certified mail on December 13, 2023, and no answer had been filed to date. Bryce indicated his intent to file a motion to consolidate the district court case into the circuit court case and offered to draft an agreed order if John had no objections to the attached motion.

- December 27, 2023, 10:23 a.m. (To: Bryce Koon; CC: Sarena Tuttle; Allan R. Bertram; Debby Bennett; Landon Cambron): John Bertram responded, Good morning. He said he had been advised that a separate matter had been filed in Barren Circuit Court, presumably arising from the same facts, and reiterated his understanding that Bryce’s firm initiated that action. He asked for confirmation and whether the matters should be consolidated. He noted a presumed difference in damages (district vs. circuit) but believed judicial economy might favor consolidation. He also asked whether an answer had been filed in the circuit matter.

- December 26–27, 2023: The emails reference an attached filing in Barren District Court (from Bryce’s December 26 message) and discuss the existence and status of a circuit court action against Jasmine Reed (Case No. 23-CI-00659) with service recorded on December 13, 2023 and no answer filed yet. The parties repeatedly considered filing a motion to consolidate the district and circuit court actions and whether an agreed order could be drafted.

- January 15, 2024, 2:34 p.m. (From: Bryce Koon; To: John Bertram; CC: Sarena Tuttle; Allan R. Bertram; Debby Bennett; Landon Cambron): Bryce wrote Good afternoon, John. He asked him to see the attached filing in Barren District Court, noting that it had been filed that day. He invited any questions.

- January 15, 2024, 7:41 p.m. (From: John D. Bertram; To: Bryce Koon; CC: Sarena Tuttle; Allan R. Bertram; Debby Bennett; Landon Cambron): John responded with simply “Thank you,” followed by his standard signature block including his phone number [PHONE-337].

Bertram (BCM LLP) and W. Bryce Koon (The Whaley Law Firm). The January 15, 2024 exchanges show the same group in the distribution.

The messages repeatedly stated they were confidential and attorney-client privileged, including standard notices about forwarding, privilege, and error handling.

- Case context and status: The note confirms the district court case, 23-C-01110, involves Debra Marshall as the defendant in a matter arising from a motor vehicle accident (Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022). The circuit court action referenced, against Jasmine Reed, is in Case No. 23-CI-00659, with service by certified mail on December 13, 2023 and no filed answer at the time of the communications. The parties discussed consolidating the district court case into the circuit court action to promote efficiency.

- The final entries (January 15, 2024) show a subsequent filing in the Barren District Court being communicated by Bryce to John, with John acknowledging receipt.

Overall, the note captures the procedural posture of late December 2023 through January 2024: a district court filing by The Whaley Law Firm related to KFBMIC, a parallel or separate circuit court action against Jasmine Reed, service on Reed without an answer, ongoing discussions about consolidating the district and circuit court proceedings, and a later January 15, 2024 filing in the district court followed by a brief acknowledgment from John Bertram. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, and John D. Bertram, Esq., with several counsel and staff copied on the messages.

On December 26, 2023, Bryce Koon sent an email to John Bertram with the subject RE: KFBMIC (a/s/o Edie Renick) v. Debra Marshall (Barren District Court 23-C-01110). Earlier in the thread, on December 27, 2023, John Bertram replied at 9:37 AM. He said he had been advised that a separate matter had been filed in Barren Circuit Court, apparently arising from the same facts, and he asked Bryce to confirm whether his understanding was correct and whether the matters should be consolidated. Bryce Koon responded at 10:02 AM the same day. Reed was served via certified mail on December 13, 2023, but no answer had been filed to date. He indicated he would inform Bryce if there was any opposition to consolidation, though he could not imagine there would be.

The thread also shows an additional message from Bryce on December 27, 2023, to John Bertram (9:37 AM) and a follow-up at 9:37 AM from Bertram, indicating ongoing discussion about consolidation and the relative timing of the actions. Earlier, on December 26, 2023, Bryce had again referenced the attached filing in Barren District Court.

Please see the attached document filed today in Barren District Court regarding the KFBMIC matter (a/s/o Edie Renick) v. Debra Marshall (23-C-01110). He asked John to let him know if there were any questions. The email was sent from The Whaley Law Firm at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with the firm’s phone and fax numbers listed. As with the prior messages, the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer appeared at the bottom of the email.

In summary, the file reflects Debra Marshall’s representation in the district court case 23-C-01110, with a parallel circuit court action against Jasmine Reed in Case No. 23-CI-00659. There were ongoing discussions about consolidating the district court case into the circuit court matter, including service on Jasmine Reed (via certified mail on [DOB-338]) and no answer filed to date, as of December 2023. On January 15, 2024, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent a good‑afternoon message to John Bertram at BCM LLP, with copies to Sarena Tuttle, Allan R. Bertram, Debby Bennett, and Landon Cambron. In that email, he wrote that he had attached documents filed that day in Barren District Court and invited Mr. Bertram to contact him with any questions. The message also included standard attorney‑client privilege language indicating the electronic communication was intended only for the named recipient and warning against disclosure if received in error. Koon’s signature block provided his firm’s name and contact information: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone (502) 365‑5043; fax (502) 364‑9363.

The sequence of prior correspondence began on December 26, 2023, when Bryce Koon emailed John Bertram with the subject noting KFBMIC v. Debra Marshall in the Barren District Court. In that message, Koon stated, “Please see attached filed today in Barren District Court,” and again attached materials were referenced along with the standard privilege notice.

He indicated that he had been advised a separate matter had been filed in Barren Circuit Court, presumably arising from the same facts, and that his understanding was that KFBMIC initiated that action. He asked for confirmation of his understanding and inquired whether he and the firm agreed that the matters should be consolidated. He noted a possible difference in damages (district vs. circuit) but suggested judicial economy might argue for consolidation, and he asked whether an answer had been filed in the matter Koon initiated.

Following Bertram’s inquiry, Bryce Koon responded on December 27, 2023 at 10:02 AM. He confirmed that Bertram’s presumptions were correct: The Whaley Law Firm had filed a circuit court action against Jasmine Reed, the driver of the Renick vehicle, in Case No. 23-CI-00659. Reed had been served via certified mail on December 13, 2023, but no answer had been filed to date. At 10:23 AM on December 27, 2023, John Bertram replied to Bryce Koon’s latest message. He said he had been informed that a separate matter had been filed in Barren Circuit Court, presumably arising from the same facts, and he reiterated his understanding that KFBMIC initiated that action. He asked whether the matters should be consolidated and suggested there might be a difference in damages between the district and circuit courts, but he believed consolidation would be appropriate for judicial economy. He also asked whether an answer had been filed in the circuit matter initiated by Koon.

On January 15, 2024, Bryce Koon sent another email to John Bertram, stating, “Good afternoon John, Please see attached filed today in Barren District Court. Please let me know if you have any questions.” The email followed the same pattern as prior communications, including the confidential/privilege notice and Koon’s firm contact details (Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone (502) 365‑5043; fax (502) 364‑9363).

In summary, the parties have been coordinating on the relationship between the district court case 23-C-01110 (Debra Marshall v. KFBMIC/Edie Renick) and a separately filed circuit court action against Jasmine Reed (driver of the Renick vehicle) in Case No. 23-CI-00659. Reed was served on December 13, 2023, by certified mail with no answer filed as of the latest communications. There has been explicit discussion of consolidating the district court case into the circuit court case, with indications that Koon would prepare an agreed order if Bertram did not object. Bertram, Debby Bennett, and Landon Cambron, and each message carried the customary attorney‑client privilege disclaimer.

item_198.note: Debra Marshall was involved in a motor vehicle accident on December 3, 2022. In late December 2023, her case surfaced in two related filings arising from that incident. The Whaley Law Firm, on behalf of KFBMIC (Kentucky Farm Bureau Mutual Insurance Company) in a matter captioned KFBMIC (a/s/0 Edie Renick) v. Debra Marshall, filed a case in Barren District Court against Debra Marshall, assigned District Court case number 23-C-01110. This action is part of the Debra Marshall MVA case referenced as Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022.

On December 26, 2023, counsel for KFBMIC advised that a circuit court action had been filed against Jasmine Reed, driver of Edie Renick’s vehicle, in the Barren Circuit Court, with Case No. 23-CI-00659. Reed was served with the circuit court action via certified mail on December 13, 2023, and, at that time, no answer had been filed. The email indicated an intent to move to consolidate the district court case into the circuit court case, and that, if there were no objections, an agreed order could be drafted.

The next day, December 27, 2023, John D. Bertram inquired by email whether the firm would be defending in the circuit court matter and whether the matters should be consolidated, noting a likely difference in damages between district court and circuit court actions but citing judicial economy as a reason to consolidate. He also asked whether an answer had been filed in the matter initiated by KFBMIC.

Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm replied on December 27, 2023, confirming that the circuit court action had indeed been filed against Jasmine Reed, Case No. 23-CI-00659, and that Reed had been served by certified mail on December 13, 2023, with no answer having been filed to date. He stated his intention to file a motion to consolidate the district court case (23-C-01110) into the circuit court case (23-CI-00659) and offered to draft an agreed order if there were no objections.

Shortly thereafter, Bertram responded that he had been advised of the separate circuit court filing arising from the same facts and asked Koon to confirm whether his understanding was correct and whether the matters should be consolidated. He again noted the potential difference in damages between district and circuit court actions but suggested consolidation could serve judicial economy, and he asked whether an answer had been filed in the matter initiated by KFBMIC.

At 10:47 a.m. on December 27, 2023, a forwarded message from Bryce Koon circulated the preceding exchange. The forwarded content reiterates Bertram’s inquiry about consolidation and reflects KFBMIC’s stance that the district court case (23-C-01110) and the circuit court case (23-CI-00659) were being coordinated, with the possibility of an agreed order if there were no objections. The message also includes the standard confidentiality disclaimer typical of communications from The Whaley Law Firm and the sender’s contact information, noting that the electronic message is intended only for the named recipient and may contain attorney-client privileged or protected information; recipients receiving the message in error are instructed to notify The Whaley Law Firm, avoid waiving privileges, and not to disclose the content to others.

In summary, in December 2023, two related actions emerged from the same underlying facts: a district court case in Barren District Court against Debra Marshall (23-C-01110) and a circuit court case against Jasmine Reed (23-CI-00659). Reed was served on December 13, 2023, with no answer filed, and counsel discussed consolidating the district and circuit court matters, with the possibility of drafting an agreed order pending any objections.

item_255.note: Case: Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022. Client: Debra Marshall. Re: Debra Marshall - Complaint Draft.

On September 27, 2023, in the Debra Marshall motor vehicle accident matter, an email thread was exchanged regarding the draft of Debra Marshall’s complaint. The message originated from Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, and was sent to Aaron Whaley with Bryce Koon and Debra Marshall cc’d. The subject line read “Re: Debra Marshall - Complaint Draft.” The header information notes the date as September 27, 2023 at 11:36:55 AM, with a -0400 time zone.

In the body of the initial note, Sarena reports that she called Cave City Police Department to obtain ORR instructions. Per Chief Miller, the department does not use dash cams or body cameras. Sarena’s signature block follows, including her role and contact details and a note indicating her email address is the new one: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com.

The thread then shows a rapid back-and-forth. Around 11:27 AM, Aaron Whaley replied with a brief “yes.” Moments earlier, at approximately 11:26 AM, Sarena asked, “Should I go ahead and send ORR for cam footage?” followed by her signature block.

Earlier still, at about 11:07 AM, Aaron advised, “Don’t file yet. I want to get a demand out. If this is a minimum policy then they may just tender. It is worth a few conversations with the adjuster.” This comment followed an earlier exchange captured in the thread.

At approximately 10:39 AM, Bryce Koon contributed, noting, “BI denied liability here ? seems like it could have some teeth but not totally sure.” He also stated that the complaint draft was attached for review, and he signed as Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm, providing his contact details.

The thread contains multiple closing sign-offs from Aaron Whaley, all identifying him as with The Whaley Law Firm at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with the firm’s phone number, [PHONE-435], repeated in the signature blocks. Debra Marshall is listed in CC on the thread, with an address associated to her Louisville incident law firm filevine app contact.

item_257.note: Case: Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022. Client: Debra Marshall. This note summarizes the email chain from September 27, 2023, concerning Debra Marshall’s motor vehicle accident case (MVA) with a December 3, 2022 incident date, and the preparation of a complaint draft.

On September 27, 2023, at 11:26:24 a.m. Eastern Time, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to Aaron Whaley (and with Bryce Koon and Debra Marshall CC’d) asking whether she should proceed to send an Open Records Request for dash-cam footage or similar camera footage. Sarena’s message preceded the firm’s internal discussion about next steps and the potential inspection of video from the scene. Her signature notes her role and includes her contact information and a new email address.

Earlier in the thread, Bryce Koon had sent a message around 10:39 a.m. noting that Bodily Injury (BI) liability had been denied and commenting that the case “seems like it could have some teeth but not totally sure.” Bryce added that the complaint draft was attached for review.

In the subsequent reply at approximately 11:04 a.m., Aaron Whaley replied that the case was a good one to file, indicating that he had saved the accident location from the police report to the case summary. He explained that a quick look at the location could show that Debra had progressed a short distance down the street before being struck. He advised obtaining open records for dash-cam or body-cam footage and expressed an interest in seeing video of the scene.

A follow-up reply around 11:07 a.m. from Aaron stated, “Don’t file yet. I want to get a demand out. If this is a minimum policy then they may just tender. It’s worth a few conversations with the adjuster.” This indicated a strategy to pursue a settlement demand before filing, depending on the policy limits and potential tender by the insurer.

The thread thus reflects a plan to file a complaint draft (with Bryce noting BI’s denial of liability and indicating the draft was attached for review), alongside consideration of obtaining open records for dash-cam or body-cam footage to illuminate the scene. The discussion also shows a strategy to first present a demand, particularly if the policy is not generous, before pursuing formal filing. Debra Marshall is the client, and her email address is included in the CC line along with the other participants. The firm’s contact details appear in the signatures, and Sarena notes a new email address.

item_305.note: Case: Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022. Client: Debra Marshall.

The notes chronicle Debra Marshall’s auto collision case and the surrounding firm communications. The file begins with an urgent follow-up thread in January 2023. On January 17, 2023, Aaron Whaley from Whaley Law Firm sent a forward titled “Debra Marshall | Urgent Follow Up Requested.” In that message, he asked that the firm reach out to Debra and instructed Debra not to communicate with the other driver’s insurance company. He noted that the other insurer had assigned fault to Debra, but he did not believe the fault was 100% on Debra and said he would handle matters with Kentucky Farm Bureau (KFB).

That same day, the message was a forward of a prior email from Farrokh Mokhtar, who was the Client Services Manager at LHP Law Group, PLLC. Mokhtar wrote that Debra had contacted them after receiving paperwork from the other driver's insurance company. He requested that Whaley’s team follow up with the insurer and also asked them to obtain the insurer’s office number for Debra. Mokhtar attached signed documents to his response. He signaled that the documents were part of the client’s intake and that a cooperative follow-up was needed. In his signature block, he identified himself and provided his contact information: Farrokh Mokhtar, Client Services Manager, LHP Law Group, PLLC, [PHONE-475] (cell), [EMAIL-476].

This January 17 thread sits atop a longer December 2022–January 2023 communication trail about Debra Marshall’s potential representation and the administrative steps involved in onboarding her case. Several earlier exchanges document notary coordination and firm onboarding. For example, on December 29–30, 2022, there was a sequence in which Debra Marshall was being integrated as a client for notary services.

- On December 29, 2022, a chain of internal and client-facing messages discussed whether Debra Marshall would be entered as a client with LHP Law Group, and whether to submit documents under LHP. A note indicated that the Express Notary Service did not have Whaley on file as a client at that time. The Express Notary representative, Luke Vafiades, replied that they did not have Whaley on file and reminded recipients about the confidential nature of the email and its attachments.

- Earlier that same day, there were communications between Jay Rodriguez (and others at Whaley Law Firm) and Farrokh Mokhtar about who would sign and how to proceed. Jay Rodriguez confirmed that Debra Marshall had agreed to a Notary appointment for tomorrow, December 30, at 10:30 a.m., confirming the address as 1224 N Dixie Hwy, Apt 1, Cave City, KY 42127, with the contact phone number [PHONE-477]. The retainer was attached to this email. The exchange also communicated the client’s English language preference.

- A message from Farrokh Mokhtar at 12:13 PM on December 30 indicated that Debra Marshall had signed with a notary that morning and that the firm would welcome her to the practice once they received the documents. Mokhtar stated he would send over the documents as soon as they were received.

- On December 29, 2022, at 2:50 PM, an alert from the Alert Call Center noted: “WHALEY POTENTIAL CLIENT – AUTO ACCIDENT (FURTHER REVIEW NEEDED).” The note left the reason for further review as partially obscured (marked “Unsure wh…” in the forwarded snippet), reflecting an initial status of uncertainty about this being Whaley’s client and about how to file the matter.

- Also on December 29, 2022, at 2:59 PM, Express Notary asked: “Hi, are we entering this as a LHP signing?” In a prior thread at 2:00 PM that day, Aaron Whaley replied, “No, Whaley Law firm.” Earlier, at 1:46 PM, Jay Rodriguez had stated that Debra Marshall had agreed to a notary appointment for 12/30 and provided the client’s details (first name Debra, last name Marshall, language English, telephone number, and address). The notary appointment details, along with the statement that the retainer had been attached, were reiterated.

- Finally, at 3:02 PM on December 29, 2022, an email from a Whaley-affiliated note asked to “submit under LHP and use the doc Jay sent over,” indicating a procedural step to route Debra’s matter through LHP Law Group’s intake and notary process, rather than the Whaley firm directly.

Taken together, these notes show that Debra Marshall’s MVA case, initially arising in early December 2022, progressed through notary onboarding and intake coordination between Whaley Law Firm and LHP Law Group, with the latter coordinating signings and the transfer of documents. By late December, Debra had agreed to a notary appointment for December 30, 2022, at 10:30 a.m. at the Cave City address provided, and the retainer was attached to the correspondence. Express Notary was involved in the process, with some questions about whether the engagement would be filed under LHP or Whaley, and a request that a notary signature be obtained and documents be exchanged.

By mid-January 2023, the emphasis shifted to urgent client outreach and insurance communications. Debra had reportedly received paperwork from the other driver's (OD’s) insurance company, prompting Farrokh Mokhtar and the LHP team to request that Whaley’s team contact the client and coordinate follow-up with the insurer, including obtaining the insurer’s office number for Debra. The January 17 communication also notes that Farrokh had attached signed documents to his reply and reiterates the plan to handle the matter with KFB, while the Whaley team prepared to engage with Debra directly and advise her to refrain from communicating with the other insurer.

In summary: Debra Marshall’s case is the Debra-Marshall-MVA-12-3-2022 file. The organizational history includes onboarding activities with LHP Law Group in December 2022, notary appointment scheduling and completion around December 29–30, 2022, and an urgent follow-up thread in January 2023 in which Whaley urged direct client contact and cautioned against contacting the other insurer, with LHP coordinating follow-up and providing signed documents to support engagement. The January 17, 2023, exchange also indicates that Debra had received paperwork from the OD’s insurer and that the team would address fault considerations (noting that Debra’s fault was not believed to be 100% hers) and would handle matters with KFB.

The location was 1224 North Dixie Hwy, Cave City, KY, in rainy and wet weather. Debra was driving a 49cc moped and was the driver of her vehicle. A witness also reported that she was on the phone at the time. Two vehicles were involved. Police and EMS responded to the scene, and EMS transported Debra to a hospital. The other driver had auto insurance, while Debra’s vehicle did not have insurance coverage. The defendant’s vehicle make and model are not specified. She was life-flighted to Nashville the same night. She received medical attention at TriStar Skyline Medical Center on 12/3/2022 and is currently being treated by Dr. Williams R T MD.
